Zartosht") of the second Sasanian [King of Kings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/King_of_Kings "King of Kings") (_[shahanshah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shah "Shah")_) [Shapur I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shapur_I "Shapur I") (r. 240–270),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBrunner1983b750_223-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBrunner1983b750-223">[220]</a></sup> which was erected in c. 262.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERapp201428_224-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-FOOTNOTERapp201428-224">[221]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-oxfordreference.com2_90-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-oxfordreference.com2-90">[87]</a></sup> The [Emesene](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emesene_dynasty "Emesene dynasty") were a dynasty of Arab priest-kings that ruled the city of [Emesa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emesa "Emesa") (modern-day [Homs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Homs "Homs"), Syria) in the [Roman province of Syria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Syria "Roman Syria") from the 1st century CE to the 3rd century CE. The dynasty is notable for producing a number of high priests of the god [El-Gabal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elagabalus "Elagabalus"), who were also influential in [Roman politics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Political_institutions_of_ancient_Rome "Political institutions of ancient Rome") and culture. The first ruler of the Emesene dynasty was [Sampsiceramus I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sampsiceramus_I "Sampsiceramus I"), who came to power in 64 CE. He was succeeded by his son, [Iamblichus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iamblichus "Iamblichus"), who was followed by his own son, [Sampsiceramus II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sampsiceramus_II "Sampsiceramus II"). Under Sampsiceramus II, Emesa became a client kingdom of the [Roman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Empire "Roman Empire"), and the dynasty became more closely tied to Roman political and cultural traditions.<sup id="cite_ref-225"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-225">[222]</a></sup>

#### Late antiquity

The [Ghassanids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghassanids "Ghassanids"), [Lakhmids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lakhmids "Lakhmids") and [Kindites](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kindites "Kindites") were the last major migration of pre-Islamic Arabs out of Yemen to the north. The Ghassanids increased the Semitic presence in then-Hellenized [Syria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syria_(Byzantine_province) "Syria (Byzantine province)"), the majority of Semites were Aramaic peoples. They mainly settled in the [Hauran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hauran "Hauran") region and spread to modern [Lebanon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lebanon "Lebanon"), [Palestine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_of_Palestine "State of Palestine") and [Jordan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jordan "Jordan"). Greeks and Romans referred to all the nomadic population of the desert in the Near East as Arabi. The Romans called Yemen "[Arabia Felix](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabia_Felix "Arabia Felix")".<sup id="cite_ref-226"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-226">[223]</a></sup> The Romans called the vassal nomadic states within the [Roman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roman_Empire "Roman Empire") _[Arabia Petraea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabia_Petraea "Arabia Petraea")_, after the city of [Petra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Petra "Petra"), and called unconquered deserts bordering the empire to the south and east [Arabia Magna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabia_Magna "Arabia Magna").

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Lakhmid.png/170px-Lakhmid.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Lakhmid.png)

Lakhmid kingdom

The [Lakhmids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lakhmids "Lakhmids") as a dynasty inherited their power from the [Tanukhids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tanukh "Tanukh"), the mid Tigris region around their capital [Al-Hira](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Hira "Al-Hira"). They ended up allying with the [Sassanids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sasanian_Empire "Sasanian Empire") against the Ghassanids and the [Byzantine Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine_Empire "Byzantine Empire"). The Lakhmids contested control of the Central Arabian tribes with the Kindites with the Lakhmids eventually destroying the [Kingdom of Kinda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kinda "Kingdom of Kinda") in 540 after the fall of their main ally [Himyar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Himyar "Himyar"). The [Persian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Persian_people "Persian people") Sassanids dissolved the Lakhmid dynasty in 602, being under puppet kings, then under their direct control.<sup id="cite_ref-227"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-227">[224]</a></sup> The Kindites migrated from Yemen along with the Ghassanids and Lakhmids, but were turned back in Bahrain by the Abdul Qais [Rabi'a](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rabi%60ah "Rabi`ah") tribe. They returned to Yemen and allied themselves with the Himyarites who installed them as a vassal kingdom that ruled Central Arabia from "Qaryah Dhat Kahl" (the present-day called Qaryat al-Faw). They ruled much of the Northern/Central Arabian peninsula, until they were destroyed by the Lakhmid king [Al-Mundhir](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Mundhir_III_ibn_al-Nu%27man "Al-Mundhir III ibn al-Nu'man"), and his son ['Amr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%27Amr_III_ibn_al-Mundhir "'Amr III ibn al-Mundhir").

The [Ghassanids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghassanids "Ghassanids") were an Arab tribe in the Levant in the early third century. According to Arab genealogical tradition, they were considered a branch of the [Azd tribe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azd "Azd"). They fought alongside the [Byzantines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine_Empire "Byzantine Empire") against the [Sasanians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sasanian_Empire "Sasanian Empire") and Arab Lakhmids. Most Ghassanids were Christians, converting to [Christianity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christianity "Christianity") in the first few centuries, and some merged with Hellenized Christian communities. After the Muslim conquest of the Levant, few Ghassanids became Muslims, and most remained Christian and joined Melkite and Syriac communities within what is now Jordan, Palestine, Syria, and Lebanon.<sup id="cite_ref-228"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-228">[225]</a></sup> The [Salihids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Salihids "Salihids") were Arab foederati in the 5th century, were ardent Christians, and their period is less documented than the preceding and succeeding periods due to a scarcity of sources. Most references to the Salihids in Arabic sources derive from the work of [Hisham ibn al-Kalbi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hisham_ibn_al-Kalbi "Hisham ibn al-Kalbi"), with the [Tarikh of Ya'qubi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tarikh_al-Yaqubi "Tarikh al-Yaqubi") considered valuable for determining the Salihids' fall and the terms of their foedus with the Byzantines.<sup id="cite_ref-229"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-229">[226]</a></sup>

### Middle Ages

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/The_Early_Muslim_Conquests_630s_to_820s.svg/417px-The_Early_Muslim_Conquests_630s_to_820s.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:The_Early_Muslim_Conquests_630s_to_820s.svg)

The early Arab conquests by reign

During the [Middle Ages](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Ages "Middle Ages"), Arab civilization flourished and the Arabs made significant contributions to the fields of [science](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Science "Science"), [mathematics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics "Mathematics"), [medicine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medicine "Medicine"), [philosophy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philosophy "Philosophy"), and [literature](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Literature "Literature"), with the rise of great cities like [Baghdad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baghdad "Baghdad"), [Cairo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cairo "Cairo"), and [Cordoba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba,_Spain "Córdoba, Spain"), they became centers of learning, attracting scholars, scientists, and intellectuals.<sup id="cite_ref-Wenner_1980_59–79_230-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Wenner_1980_59%E2%80%9379-230">[227]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-A_Golden_age_of_Arab_culture_231-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-A_Golden_age_of_Arab_culture-231">[228]</a></sup> Arabs forged many empires and dynasties, most notably, the Rashidun Empire, the Umayyad Empire, the Abbasid Empire, the Fatimid Empire, among others. These empires were characterized by their expansion, scientific achievements, and cultural flourishing, extended from [Spain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spain "Spain") to [India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India "India").<sup id="cite_ref-Wenner_1980_59–79_230-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Wenner_1980_59%E2%80%9379-230">[227]</a></sup> The region was vibrant and dynamic during the Middle Ages and left a lasting impact on the world.<sup id="cite_ref-A_Golden_age_of_Arab_culture_231-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-A_Golden_age_of_Arab_culture-231">[228]</a></sup>

![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/timeline/ifmyqrmejd4hnvo52cmbalxfdhesiq4.png)

The [rise of Islam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spread_of_Islam "Spread of Islam") began when [Muhammad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad "Muhammad") and his followers migrated from [Mecca](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mecca "Mecca") to [Medina](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medina "Medina") in an event known as the [Hijra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hijrah "Hijrah"). Muhammad spent the last ten years of his life engaged in a series of battles to establish and expand the Muslim community. From 622 to 632, he led the Muslims in a state of war against the Meccans.<sup id="cite_ref-Collins142_232-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Collins142-232">[229]</a></sup> During this period, the Arabs conquered the region of [Basra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basra "Basra"), and under the leadership of [Umar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umar "Umar"), they established a base and built a mosque there. Another conquest was [Midian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Midian "Midian"), but due to its harsh environment, the settlers eventually moved to [Kufa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kufa "Kufa"). Umar successfully defeated rebellions by various Arab tribes, bringing stability to the entire Arabian peninsula and unifying it. Under the leadership of [Uthman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uthman "Uthman"), the Arab empire expanded through the [conquest of Persia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_conquest_of_Persia "Arab conquest of Persia"), with the capture of Fars in 650 and parts of [Khorasan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khorasan_province "Khorasan province") in 651.<sup id="cite_ref-Cunliffe4212_233-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Cunliffe4212-233">[230]</a></sup> The [conquest of Armenia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_conquest_of_armenia "Arab conquest of armenia") also began in the 640s. During this time, the Rashidun Empire extended its rule over the entire [Sassanid Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sasanian_Empire "Sasanian Empire") and more than two-thirds of the [Eastern Roman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine_Empire "Byzantine Empire"). However, the reign of [Ali ibn Abi Talib](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ali "Ali"), the fourth caliph, was marred by the [First Fitna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/First_Fitna "First Fitna"), or the First Islamic Civil War, which lasted throughout his rule. After a peace treaty with [Hassan ibn Ali](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hasan_ibn_Ali "Hasan ibn Ali") and the suppression of early [Kharijite](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kharijites "Kharijites") disturbances, [Muawiyah I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mu%27awiya_I "Mu'awiya I") became the Caliph.<sup id="cite_ref-Brown15_234-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Brown15-234">[231]</a></sup> This marked a significant transition in leadership.<sup id="cite_ref-Cunliffe4212_233-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Cunliffe4212-233">[230]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Collins376_235-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Collins376-235">[232]</a></sup>

#### Arab empires

##### Rashidun era (632–661)

After the death of [Muhammad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad "Muhammad") in 632, [Rashidun armies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rashidun_army "Rashidun army") launched campaigns of conquest, establishing the [Caliphate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caliphate "Caliphate"), or Islamic Empire, one of the [largest empires in history](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_largest_empires "List of largest empires"). It was larger and lasted longer than the previous Arab empire [Tanukhids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tanukhids "Tanukhids") of [Queen Mawia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mavia_(queen) "Mavia (queen)") or the Arab [Palmyrene Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palmyrene_Empire "Palmyrene Empire"). The Rashidun state was a completely new state and unlike the Arab kingdoms of its century such as the [Himyarite](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Himyarite "Himyarite"), [Lakhmids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lakhmids "Lakhmids") or [Ghassanids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghassanids "Ghassanids").

During the Rashidun era, the Arab community expanded rapidly, conquering many territories and establishing a vast Arab empire, which is marked by the reign of the first four caliphs, or leaders, of the Arab community.<sup id="cite_ref-Understanding_Islam:_The_First_Ten_Steps_236-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Understanding_Islam:_The_First_Ten_Steps-236">[233]</a></sup> These caliphs are [Abu Bakr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abu_Bakr "Abu Bakr"), [Umar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umar "Umar"), [Uthman](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Uthman "Uthman") and [Ali](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ali "Ali"), who are collectively known as the Rashidun, meaning "rightly guided." The Rashidun era is significant in Arab and Islamic history as it marks the beginning of the Arab empire and the [spread of Islam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spread_of_Islam "Spread of Islam") beyond the Arabian Peninsula. During this time, the Arab community faced numerous challenges, including internal divisions and external threats from neighboring empires.<sup id="cite_ref-Understanding_Islam:_The_First_Ten_Steps_236-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Understanding_Islam:_The_First_Ten_Steps-236">[233]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Triana_159_237-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Triana_159-237">[234]</a></sup>

Under the leadership of Abu Bakr, the Arab community successfully quelled a [rebellion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rebellion "Rebellion") by some tribes who refused to pay [Zakat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zakat "Zakat"), or Islamic charity. During the reign of Umar ibn al-Khattab, the Arab empire expanded significantly, conquering territories such as Egypt, [Syria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syria "Syria"), and [Iraq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq "Iraq"). The reign of Uthman ibn Affan was marked by internal dissent and rebellion, which ultimately led to his assassination. Ali, the cousin and son-in-law of [Muhammad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad "Muhammad"), succeeded Uthman as caliph but faced opposition from some members of the Islamic community who believed he was not rightfully appointed.<sup id="cite_ref-Understanding_Islam:_The_First_Ten_Steps_236-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Understanding_Islam:_The_First_Ten_Steps-236">[233]</a></sup> Despite these challenges, the Rashidun era is remembered as a time of great progress and achievement in Arab and Islamic history, the caliphs established a system of governance that emphasized [justice](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Justice "Justice") and equality for all members of the Islamic community. They also oversaw the compilation of the Quran into a single text and spread Arabic teachings and principles throughout the empire. Overall, the Rashidun era played a crucial role in shaping Arab history and continues to be revered by Muslims worldwide as a period of exemplary leadership and guidance.<sup id="cite_ref-238"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-238">[235]</a></sup>

##### Umayyad era (661–750 & 756–1031)

In 661, the Rashidun Caliphate fell into the hands of the [Umayyad dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Banu_Umayya "Banu Umayya") and [Damascus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Damascus "Damascus") was established as the empire's capital. The Umayyads were proud of their Arab identity and sponsored the poetry and culture of pre-Islamic Arabia. They established garrison towns at [Ramla](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ramla "Ramla"), [Raqqa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raqqa "Raqqa"), [Basra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basra "Basra"), [Kufa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kufa "Kufa"), [Mosul](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mosul "Mosul") and [Samarra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samarra "Samarra"), all of which developed into major cities.<sup id="cite_ref-Lunde_239-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Lunde-239">[236]</a></sup> [Caliph](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caliph "Caliph") [Abd al-Malik](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abd_al-Malik_ibn_Marwan "Abd al-Malik ibn Marwan") established Arabic as the Caliphate's official language in 686.<sup id="cite_ref-240"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-240">[237]</a></sup> Caliph [Umar II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umar_II "Umar II") strove to resolve the conflict when he came to power in 717. He rectified the disparity, demanding that all Muslims be treated as equals, but his intended reforms did not take effect, as he died after only three years of rule. By now, discontent with the Umayyads swept the region and an uprising occurred in which the [Abbasids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphate "Abbasid Caliphate") came to power and moved the capital to [Baghdad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baghdad "Baghdad").

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/La_civilitzaci%C3%B3_del_califat_de_C%C3%B2rdova_en_temps_d%27Abd-al-Rahman_III.jpg/220px-La_civilitzaci%C3%B3_del_califat_de_C%C3%B2rdova_en_temps_d%27Abd-al-Rahman_III.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:La_civilitzaci%C3%B3_del_califat_de_C%C3%B2rdova_en_temps_d%27Abd-al-Rahman_III.jpg)

The [Caliphate of Còrdova](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caliphate_of_C%C3%B3rdoba "Caliphate of Córdoba") during the reign of [Abd al-Rahman III](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abd_al-Rahman_III "Abd al-Rahman III"). Receiving the Ambassador by [Dionisio Baixeras Verdaguer](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dionisio_Baixeras_Verdaguer "Dionisio Baixeras Verdaguer") 1885 CE.

Umayyads expanded their Empire westwards capturing North Africa from the Byzantines. Before the Arab conquest, North Africa was conquered or settled by various people including [Punics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Punics "Punics"), Vandals and Romans. After the [Abbasid Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abbasid_Revolution "Abbasid Revolution"), the Umayyads lost most of their territories with the exception of Iberia.

Their last holding became known as the [Emirate of Córdoba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emirate_of_C%C3%B3rdoba "Emirate of Córdoba"). It was not until the rule of the grandson of the founder of this new emirate that the state entered a new phase as the [Caliphate of Córdoba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caliphate_of_C%C3%B3rdoba "Caliphate of Córdoba"). This new state was characterized by an expansion of trade, culture and knowledge, and saw the construction of masterpieces of [al-Andalus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Andalus "Al-Andalus") architecture and the library of [Al-Ḥakam II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-%E1%B8%A4akam_II "Al-Ḥakam II") which housed over 400,000 volumes. With the collapse of the Umayyad state in 1031 CE, [Al-Andalus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Andalus "Al-Andalus") was divided into [small kingdoms](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taifa "Taifa").<sup id="cite_ref-241"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-241">[238]</a></sup>

##### Abbasid era (750–1258 and 1261–1517)

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Harun_al-Rashid_receives_envoys_from_Charlemagne.jpg/221px-Harun_al-Rashid_receives_envoys_from_Charlemagne.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Harun_al-Rashid_receives_envoys_from_Charlemagne.jpg)

[Harun al-Rashid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harun_al-Rashid "Harun al-Rashid") ([r.](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reign "Reign") 786–809) receiving a delegation sent by [Charlemagne](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charlemagne "Charlemagne") at his court in Baghdad.

The Abbasids were the descendants of [Abbas ibn Abd al-Muttalib](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Abbas_ibn_Abd_al-Muttalib "Al-Abbas ibn Abd al-Muttalib"), one of the youngest uncles of Muhammad and of the same [Banu Hashim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Banu_Hashim "Banu Hashim") clan. The Abbasids led a revolt against the Umayyads and defeated them in the [Battle of the Zab](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_the_Zab "Battle of the Zab") effectively ending their rule in all parts of the Empire with the exception of al-Andalus. In 762, the second Abbasid Caliph [al-Mansur](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Mansur "Al-Mansur") founded the city of [Baghdad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baghdad "Baghdad") and declared it the capital of the Caliphate. Unlike the Umayyads, the Abbasids had the support of non-Arab subjects.<sup id="cite_ref-Lunde_239-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Lunde-239">[236]</a></sup> The [Islamic Golden Age](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age "Islamic Golden Age") was inaugurated by the middle of the 8th century by the ascension of the Abbasid Caliphate and the transfer of the capital from [Damascus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Damascus "Damascus") to the newly founded city of [Baghdad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baghdad "Baghdad"). The Abbasids were influenced by the [Quranic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quran "Quran") injunctions and [hadith](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hadith "Hadith") such as "The ink of the scholar is more holy than the blood of martyrs" stressing the value of knowledge.

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/001124-MalwiyaMosque-Samerra-IMG_7824-2.jpg/200px-001124-MalwiyaMosque-Samerra-IMG_7824-2.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:001124-MalwiyaMosque-Samerra-IMG_7824-2.jpg)

Malwiyah Mosque, [Samerra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Samarra "Samarra"), [Iraq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq "Iraq")

During this period the Arab Empire became an intellectual centre for science, philosophy, medicine and education as the Abbasids championed the cause of knowledge and established the "[House of Wisdom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/House_of_Wisdom "House of Wisdom")" ([Arabic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabic_language "Arabic language"): بيت الحكمة) in Baghdad. Rival dynasties such as the [Fatimids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fatimid "Fatimid") of [Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egypt "Egypt") and the [Umayyads](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umayyad "Umayyad") of al-Andalus were also major intellectual centres with cities such as [Cairo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cairo "Cairo") and [Córdoba](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba,_Spain "Córdoba, Spain") rivaling [Baghdad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baghdad "Baghdad").<sup id="cite_ref-Vartan_242-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Vartan-242">[239]</a></sup> The Abbasids ruled for 200 years before they lost their central control when [Wilayas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wilayah "Wilayah") began to fracture in the 10th century; afterwards, in the 1190s, there was a revival of their power, which was ended by the [Mongols](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mongol_Empire "Mongol Empire"), who [conquered Baghdad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Baghdad_(1258) "Siege of Baghdad (1258)") in 1258 and killed the Caliph [Al-Musta'sim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Musta%27sim "Al-Musta'sim"). Members of the Abbasid royal family escaped the massacre and resorted to Cairo, which had broken from the Abbasid rule two years earlier; the [Mamluk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mamluk_Sultanate_(Cairo) "Mamluk Sultanate (Cairo)") generals taking the political side of the kingdom while Abbasid Caliphs were engaged in civil activities and continued patronizing science, arts and literature.

##### Fatimid era (909–1171)

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Skylitzes_Simeon_sending_envoys_to_the_Fatimids.jpg/200px-Skylitzes_Simeon_sending_envoys_to_the_Fatimids.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Skylitzes_Simeon_sending_envoys_to_the_Fatimids.jpg)

Bulgarian emperor [Simeon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simeon_I_of_Bulgaria "Simeon I of Bulgaria") (left) sending envoys to Caliph al-Mahdi (right). 12th-century miniature from the _[Madrid Skylitzes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Madrid_Skylitzes "Madrid Skylitzes")_

The Fatimid caliphate was founded by [al-Mahdi Billah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdullah_al-Mahdi_Billah "Abdullah al-Mahdi Billah"), a descendant of [Fatimah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fatimah "Fatimah"), the daughter of Muhammad, the Fatimid Caliphate was a [Shia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shia_Islam "Shia Islam") that existed from 909 to 1171 CE. The empire was based in North Africa, with its capital in [Cairo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cairo "Cairo"), and at its height, it controlled a vast territory that included parts of modern-day [Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egypt "Egypt"), [Libya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Libya "Libya"), [Tunisia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tunisia "Tunisia"), [Algeria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algeria "Algeria"), [Morocco](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morocco "Morocco"), [Syria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syria "Syria"), and [Palestine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestine_(region) "Palestine (region)"). The Fatimid state took shape among the [Kutama](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kutama "Kutama"), in the West of the North African littoral, in Algeria, in 909 conquering [Raqqada](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raqqada "Raqqada"), the [Aghlabid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aghlabid "Aghlabid") capital. In 921 the Fatimids established the Tunisian city of [Mahdia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahdia "Mahdia") as their new capital. In 948 they shifted their capital to [Al-Mansuriya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mansouria,_Tunisia "Mansouria, Tunisia"), near [Kairouan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kairouan "Kairouan") in Tunisia, and in 969 they conquered Egypt and established Cairo as the capital of their caliphate.

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Azhar_mosque.jpg/200px-Azhar_mosque.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Azhar_mosque.jpg)

[Al-Azhar Mosque](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Azhar_Mosque "Al-Azhar Mosque") in [Cairo, Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cairo "Cairo") in the [historic Islamic core of the city](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Cairo "Islamic Cairo"), Cairo was established as the new capital of the [Fatimid Caliphate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fatimid_Caliphate "Fatimid Caliphate") in 970

The Fatimids were known for their religious tolerance and intellectual achievements, they established a network of universities and libraries that became centers of learning in the [Islamic world](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim_world "Muslim world"). They also promoted the arts, architecture, and literature, which flourished under their patronage. One of the most notable achievements of the Fatimids was the construction of the [Al-Azhar Mosque](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Azhar_Mosque "Al-Azhar Mosque") and [Al-Azhar University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Azhar_University "Al-Azhar University") in Cairo. Founded in 970 CE, it is one of the oldest universities in the world and remains an important center of Islamic learning to this day. The Fatimids also had a significant impact on the development of [Islamic theology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Schools_of_Islamic_theology "Schools of Islamic theology") and [jurisprudence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fiqh "Fiqh"). They were known for their support of Shia Islam and their promotion of the [Ismaili](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isma%27ilism "Isma'ilism") branch of Shia Islam. Despite their many achievements, the Fatimids faced numerous challenges during their reign. They were constantly at war with neighboring empires, including the Abbasid Caliphate and the [Byzantine Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Byzantine_Empire "Byzantine Empire"). They also faced internal conflicts and rebellions, which weakened their empire over time. In 1171 CE, the Fatimid Caliphate was conquered by the [Ayyubid dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ayyubid_dynasty "Ayyubid dynasty"), led by [Saladin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saladin "Saladin"). Although the Fatimid dynasty came to an end, its legacy continued to influence Arab-Islamic culture and society for centuries to come.<sup id="cite_ref-imamreza.net_243-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-imamreza.net-243">[240]</a></sup>

##### Ottoman era (1517–1918)

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Sharif_Hussein_portrait.jpeg/144px-Sharif_Hussein_portrait.jpeg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Sharif_Hussein_portrait.jpeg)

[Hussein bin Ali al-Hashimi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz "Hussein bin Ali, King of Hejaz") (1854-1931) was a prominent Arab leader who served as the [Sharif](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sharifian_Solution "Sharifian Solution") and [Emir of Mecca](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sharif_of_Mecca "Sharif of Mecca") from 1908 until 1917. He was a member of the [Hashemite dynasty](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hashemites "Hashemites"), which claimed descent from [Muhammad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad "Muhammad").

From 1517 to 1918, The Ottomans defeated the [Mamluk Sultanate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mamluk_Sultanate_(Cairo) "Mamluk Sultanate (Cairo)") in Cairo, and ended the Abbasid Caliphate in the battles of [Marj Dabiq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Marj_Dabiq "Battle of Marj Dabiq") and [Ridaniya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Battle_of_Ridaniya "Battle of Ridaniya"). They entered the [Levant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Levant "Levant") and Egypt as conquerors, and brought down the Abbasid caliphate after it lasted for many centuries. In 1911, Arab intellectuals and politicians from throughout the Levant formed al-Fatat ("the [Young Arab Society](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Young_Arab_Society "Young Arab Society")"), a small Arab nationalist club, in Paris. Its stated aim was "raising the level of the [Arab nation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Nationalist_Movement "Arab Nationalist Movement") to the level of modern nations." In the first few years of its existence, al-Fatat called for greater autonomy within a unified Ottoman state rather than Arab independence from the empire. Al-Fatat hosted the [Arab Congress of 1913](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Congress_of_1913 "Arab Congress of 1913") in Paris, the purpose of which was to discuss desired reforms with other dissenting individuals from the Arab world.<sup id="cite_ref-244"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-244">[241]</a></sup> However, as the Ottoman authorities cracked down on the organization's activities and members, al-Fatat went underground and demanded the complete independence and unity of the Arab provinces.<sup id="cite_ref-Choueiri166_245-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Choueiri166-245">[242]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/MPK1-426_Sykes_Picot_Agreement_Map_signed_8_May_1916.jpg/200px-MPK1-426_Sykes_Picot_Agreement_Map_signed_8_May_1916.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:MPK1-426_Sykes_Picot_Agreement_Map_signed_8_May_1916.jpg)

The region covered by the modus vivendi, as agreed in the 1916 Sykes–Picot Agreement

The [Arab Revolt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Revolt "Arab Revolt") was a military uprising of Arab forces against the Ottoman Empire during World War I, began in 1916, led by [Sherif Hussein bin Ali](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz "Hussein bin Ali, King of Hejaz"), the goal of the revolt was to gain independence for the Arab lands under Ottoman rule and to create a unified Arab state. The revolt was sparked by a number of factors, including the Arab desire for greater autonomy within the Ottoman Empire, resentment towards Ottoman policies, and the influence of Arab nationalist movements. The Arab Revolt was a significant factor in the eventual [defeat of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_Ottoman_Empire "Dissolution of the Ottoman Empire"). The revolt helped to weaken Ottoman military power and tie up Ottoman forces that could have been deployed elsewhere. It also helped to increase support for Arab independence and nationalism, which would have a lasting impact on the region in the years to come.<sup id="cite_ref-246"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-246">[243]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-247"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-247">[244]</a></sup> The Empire's defeat and the occupation of part of its territory by the [Allied Powers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I "Allies of World War I") in the [aftermath of World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aftermath_of_World_War_I "Aftermath of World War I"), the [Sykes–Picot Agreement](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sykes%E2%80%93Picot_Agreement "Sykes–Picot Agreement") had a significant impact on the Arab world and its people. The agreement divided the Arab territories of the Ottoman Empire into zones of control for France and Britain, ignoring the aspirations of the Arab people for independence and self-determination.<sup id="cite_ref-248"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-248">[245]</a></sup>

### Renaissance

The Golden Age of Arab Civilization known as the "_[Islamic Golden Age](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age "Islamic Golden Age")_", traditionally dated from the 8th century to the 13th century.<sup id="cite_ref-Saliba_249-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Saliba-249">[246]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-King_250-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-King-250">[247]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hassan-Decline_251-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Hassan-Decline-251">[248]</a></sup> The period is traditionally said to have ended with the collapse of the Abbasid caliphate due to [Siege of Baghdad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Siege_of_Baghdad_(1258) "Siege of Baghdad (1258)") in 1258.<sup id="cite_ref-Tahir_Abbas_252-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Tahir_Abbas-252">[249]</a></sup> During this time, [Arab scholars](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_pre-modern_Arab_scientists_and_scholars "List of pre-modern Arab scientists and scholars") made significant contributions to fields such as mathematics, astronomy, medicine, and philosophy. These advancements had a profound impact on European scholars during the [Renaissance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Renaissance "Renaissance").<sup id="cite_ref-253"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-253">[250]</a></sup>

The Arabs shared its knowledge and ideas with [Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Europe "Europe"), including translations of Arabic texts.<sup id="cite_ref-254"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-254">[251]</a></sup> These translations had a significant impact on [culture of Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Culture_of_Europe "Culture of Europe"), leading to the transformation of many philosophical disciplines in the [medieval Latin world](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medieval_Latin "Medieval Latin"). Additionally, the Arabs made original innovations in various fields, including the arts, [agriculture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Agricultural_Revolution "Arab Agricultural Revolution"), [alchemy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alchemy "Alchemy"), [music](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Music "Music"), and [pottery](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pottery "Pottery"), and [traditional star names](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Arabic_star_names "List of Arabic star names") such as [Aldebaran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aldebaran "Aldebaran"), scientific terms like _[alchemy](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/alchemy "wiktionary:alchemy")_ (whence also _[chemistry](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/chemistry "wiktionary:chemistry")_), _[algebra](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/algebra "wiktionary:algebra")_, _[algorithm](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/algorithm "wiktionary:algorithm")_, etc. and names of commodities such as _[sugar](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/sugar "wiktionary:sugar")_, _[camphor](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/camphor "wiktionary:camphor")_, _[cotton](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cotton "wiktionary:cotton")_, _[coffee](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/coffee "wiktionary:coffee")_, etc.<sup id="cite_ref-255"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-255">[252]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-256"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-256">[253]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-257"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-257">[254]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-258"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-258">[255]</a></sup>

From the medieval scholars of the [Renaissance of the 12th century](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Renaissance_of_the_12th_century "Renaissance of the 12th century"), who had focused on studying [Greek](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_language "Greek language") and [Arabic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabic "Arabic") works of natural sciences, philosophy, and mathematics, rather than on such cultural texts. Arab logician, most notably [Averroes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Averroes "Averroes"), had inherited Greek ideas after they had invaded and conquered [Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_Egypt "Muslim conquest of Egypt") and the [Levant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim_conquest_of_the_Levant "Muslim conquest of the Levant"). Their translations and commentaries on these ideas worked their way through the Arab West into [Iberia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Andalus "Al-Andalus") and [Sicily](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emirate_of_Sicily "Emirate of Sicily"), which became important centers for this transmission of ideas. From the 11th to the 13th century, many schools dedicated to the translation of philosophical and scientific works from [Classical Arabic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Classical_Arabic "Classical Arabic") to [Medieval Latin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medieval_Latin "Medieval Latin") were established in Iberia, most notably the [Toledo School of Translators](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Toledo_School_of_Translators "Toledo School of Translators"). This work of translation from Arab culture, though largely unplanned and disorganized, constituted one of the greatest transmissions of ideas in history.<sup id="cite_ref-259"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-259">[256]</a></sup>

During the [Timurid Renaissance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Timurid_Renaissance "Timurid Renaissance") spanning the late 14th, the 15th, and the early 16th centuries, there was a significant exchange of ideas, art, and knowledge between different cultures and civilizations. Arab scholars, artists, and intellectuals played a role in this cultural exchange, contributing to the overall intellectual atmosphere of the time. They participated in various fields, including literature, art, science, and philosophy.<sup id="cite_ref-260"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-260">[257]</a></sup> In the late 19th and early 20th centuries, the [Arab Renaissance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Renaissance "Arab Renaissance"), also known as the Nahda, was a cultural and intellectual movement that emerged. The term "Nahda" means "awakening" or "renaissance" in Arabic, and refers to a period of renewed interest in Arabic language, literature, and culture.<sup id="cite_ref-Sheehi2004_261-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Sheehi2004-261">[258]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-262"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-262">[259]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Pacini1998_263-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Pacini1998-263">[260]</a></sup>

### Modern period

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Arab_League-Map-WS.PNG/350px-Arab_League-Map-WS.PNG)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Arab_League-Map-WS.PNG)

A map of the Arab world, formally the **Arab homeland**; also known as the **Arab nation.**

The modern period in [Arab history](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Arabs "History of the Arabs") refers to the time period from the late 19th century to the present day. During this time, the [Arab world](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_world "Arab world") experienced significant [political](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Politics "Politics"), [economic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Economy "Economy"), and social changes. One of the most significant events of the modern period was the collapse of the Ottoman Empire, the end of Ottoman rule led to the emergence of new [nation-states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nation_state "Nation state") in the Arab world.<sup id="cite_ref-264"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-264">[261]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-265"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-265">[262]</a></sup>

Sharif Hussein was supposed, in the event of the success of the Arab revolution and the victory of the [Allies in World War I](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_I "Allies of World War I"), to be able to establish an independent Arab state consisting of the Arabian Peninsula and the Fertile Crescent, including Iraq and the Levant. He aimed to become "King of the Arabs" in this state, however, the Arab revolution only succeeded in achieving some of its objectives, including the [independence of the Hejaz](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hejaz "Kingdom of Hejaz") and the recognition of Sharif Hussein as its king by the Allies.<sup id="cite_ref-266"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-266">[263]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Algunos_miembros_de_Al-Rabita_al-Qalamiyya.jpg/165px-Algunos_miembros_de_Al-Rabita_al-Qalamiyya.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Algunos_miembros_de_Al-Rabita_al-Qalamiyya.jpg)

A 1920 photograph of four prominent members of [The Pen League](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mahjar "Mahjar") literal meanings being "the [Arab diaspora](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_diaspora "Arab diaspora")"<sup id="cite_ref-267"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-267">[264]</a></sup> predecessors in the Nahda movement (or the "[Arab Renaissance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nahda "Nahda")"). (From left to right): [Nasib Arida](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nasib_Arida "Nasib Arida"), [Kahlil Gibran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kahlil_Gibran "Kahlil Gibran"), [Abd al-Masih Haddad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abd_al-Masih_Haddad "Abd al-Masih Haddad"), and [Mikhail Naimy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mikhail_Naimy "Mikhail Naimy").

[Arab nationalism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_nationalism "Arab nationalism") emerged as a major movement in the early 20th century, with many Arab intellectuals, artists, and political leaders seeking to promote unity and independence for the Arab world.<sup id="cite_ref-Requiem_268-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Requiem-268">[265]</a></sup> This movement gained momentum after [World War II](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/World_War_II "World War II"), leading to the formation of the Arab League and the creation of several new Arab states. [Pan-Arabism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pan-Arabism "Pan-Arabism") that emerged in the early 20th century and aimed to unite all Arabs into a single [nation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nation "Nation") or state. It emphasized on a shared [ancestry, culture, history, language and identity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_identity "Arab identity") and sought to create a sense of pan-Arab identity and solidarity.<sup id="cite_ref-smith_269-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-smith-269">[266]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Sela151_270-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Sela151-270">[267]</a></sup>

The roots of pan-Arabism can be traced back to the [Arab Renaissance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nahda "Nahda") or Al-Nahda movement of the late 19th century, which saw a revival of Arab culture, literature, and intellectual thought. The movement emphasized the importance of Arab unity and the need to resist colonialism and foreign domination. One of the key figures in the development of pan-Arabism was the Egyptian statesman and intellectual, [Gamal Abdel Nasser](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gamal_Abdel_Nasser "Gamal Abdel Nasser"), who led the [1952 revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1952_Egyptian_Revolution "1952 Egyptian Revolution") in Egypt and became the country's president in 1954. Nasser promoted pan-Arabism as a means of strengthening Arab solidarity and resisting Western imperialism. He also supported the idea of [Arab socialism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_socialism "Arab socialism"), which sought to combine pan-Arabism with socialist principles. Similar attempts were made by other [Arab leaders](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_leaders_of_Middle_Eastern_and_North_African_states#Leaders_of_Arab_League_member_states "List of leaders of Middle Eastern and North African states"), such as [Hafiz al-Assad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hafiz_al-Assad "Hafiz al-Assad"), [Ahmed Hassan al-Bakr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahmed_Hassan_al-Bakr "Ahmed Hassan al-Bakr"), [Faisal I of Iraq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Faisal_I_of_Iraq "Faisal I of Iraq"), [Muammar Gaddafi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muammar_Gaddafi "Muammar Gaddafi"), [Saddam Hussein](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saddam_Hussein "Saddam Hussein"), [Gaafar Nimeiry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaafar_Nimeiry "Gaafar Nimeiry") and [Anwar Sadat](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anwar_Sadat "Anwar Sadat").<sup id="cite_ref-271"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-271">[268]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Flag_of_Hejaz_1917.svg/161px-Flag_of_Hejaz_1917.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Flag_of_Hejaz_1917.svg)

The [flag](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flag_of_the_Arab_Revolt "Flag of the Arab Revolt") of the [Arab Revolt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Revolt "Arab Revolt") against the [Ottoman Empire](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_Empire "Ottoman Empire") is a prominent symbol of Arab nationalism. Its design and [colors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pan-Arab_colors "Pan-Arab colors") are the basis of many of the [Arab states](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_states "Arab states")' [flags](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Arab_flags "List of Arab flags"). The [Pan-Arab colors](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pan-Arab_colors "Pan-Arab colors") are [black](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Black "Black"), [white](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/White "White"), [green](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green "Green") and [red](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red "Red"). Individually, each of the four Pan-Arab colors were intended to represent a certain aspect of the Arabs and their history.

Many proposed unions aimed to create a [unified Arab](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Union "Arab Union") entity that would promote cooperation and integration among Arab countries. However, the initiatives faced numerous challenges and obstacles, including political divisions, regional conflicts, and economic disparities.<sup id="cite_ref-feb1_272-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-feb1-272">[269]</a></sup> The [United Arab Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Arab_Republic "United Arab Republic") (UAR) was a political union formed between Egypt and Syria in 1958, with the goal of creating a federal structure that would allow each member state to retain its identity and institutions. However, by 1961, Syria had withdrawn from the UAR due to political differences, and Egypt continued to call itself the UAR until 1971, when it became the [Arab Republic of Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egypt "Egypt"). In the same year the UAR was formed, another proposed political union, the [Arab Federation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Federation "Arab Federation"), was established between [Jordan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jordan "Jordan") and [Iraq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq "Iraq"), but it collapsed after only six months due to tensions with the UAR and the [14 July Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/14_July_Revolution "14 July Revolution"). A confederation called the [United Arab States](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Arab_States "United Arab States"), which included the UAR and the [Mutawakkilite Kingdom of Yemen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mutawakkilite_Kingdom_of_Yemen "Mutawakkilite Kingdom of Yemen"), was also created in 1958 but dissolved in 1961.<sup id="cite_ref-Continuum_273-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Continuum-273">[270]</a></sup> Later attempts to create a political and economic union among Arab countries included the [Federation of Arab Republics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federation_of_Arab_Republics "Federation of Arab Republics"), which was formed by Egypt, [Libya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Libya "Libya"), and Syria in the 1970s but dissolved after five years due to political and economic challenges. Muammar Gaddafi, the leader of Libya, also proposed the [Arab Islamic Republic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Islamic_Republic "Arab Islamic Republic") with Tunisia, aiming to include [Algeria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algeria "Algeria") and [Morocco](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morocco "Morocco"),<sup id="cite_ref-274"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-274">[271]</a></sup> instead the [Arab Maghreb Union](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Maghreb_Union "Arab Maghreb Union") was formed in 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-275"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-275">[272]</a></sup>

During the latter half of the 20th century, many Arab countries experienced political upheaval and conflicts, including, revolutions. The [Arab-Israeli conflict](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab%E2%80%93Israeli_conflict "Arab–Israeli conflict") remains a major issue in the region, and has resulted in ongoing tensions and periodic outbreaks of violence. In recent years, the Arab world has faced new challenges, including economic and social inequalities, demographic changes, and the impact of [globalization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Globalization "Globalization").<sup id="cite_ref-276"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-276">[273]</a></sup> The [Arab Spring](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Spring "Arab Spring") was a series of pro-democracy uprisings and protests that swept across several countries in the Arab world in 2010 and 2011. The uprisings were sparked by a combination of political, economic, and social grievances and called for democratic reforms and an end to authoritarian rule. While the protests resulted in the downfall of some long-time authoritarian leaders, they also led to ongoing conflicts and political instability in other countries.<sup id="cite_ref-277"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-277">[274]</a></sup>

## Identity

[![Costumes of Arab men, fourth to sixth century](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/PLATE8DX_foruth_sixth.jpg/152px-PLATE8DX_foruth_sixth.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:PLATE8DX_foruth_sixth.jpg)

[![Costumes of Arab women, fourth to sixth century.](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/PLATE8CX.jpg/152px-PLATE8CX.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:PLATE8CX.jpg)

Artistic rendering of pre-Islamic costumes of Arab men and Arab women between fourth to sixth century

Arab identity is defined independently of [religious](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Religion "Religion") identity, and pre-dates the [spread of Islam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spread_of_Islam "Spread of Islam"), with historically attested [Arab Christian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Christians "Arab Christians") kingdoms and [Arab Jewish tribes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jewish_tribes_of_Arabia "Jewish tribes of Arabia"). Today, however, most Arabs are Muslim, with a minority adhering to other faiths, largely [Christianity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Christianity_in_the_Middle_East "Christianity in the Middle East"), but also [Druze](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Druze "Druze") and [Baháʼí](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith "Baháʼí Faith").<sup id="cite_ref-278"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-278">[275]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-279"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-279">[276]</a></sup> Paternal descent has traditionally been considered the main source of affiliation in the [Arab world](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_world "Arab world") when it comes to membership into an [ethnic group](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnicity "Ethnicity") or [clan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Clan "Clan").<sup id="cite_ref-280"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-280">[277]</a></sup>

Arab identity is shaped by a range of factors, including ancestry, history, language, customs, and traditions.<sup id="cite_ref-281"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-281">[278]</a></sup> Arab identity has been shaped by a rich history that includes the rise and fall of [empires](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Empire "Empire"), [colonization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Colonization "Colonization"), and political turmoil. Despite the challenges faced by Arab communities, their shared cultural heritage has helped to maintain a sense of unity and pride in their identity.<sup id="cite_ref-Imagining_the_Arabs_:_Arab_identity_and_the_rise_of_Islam_282-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Imagining_the_Arabs_:_Arab_identity_and_the_rise_of_Islam-282">[279]</a></sup> Today, Arab identity continues to evolve as Arab communities navigate complex political, social, and economic landscapes. Despite this, the Arab identity remains an important aspect of the cultural and historical fabric of the Arab world, and continues to be celebrated and preserved by [communities around the world](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_diaspora "Arab diaspora").<sup id="cite_ref-283"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-283">[280]</a></sup>

## Subgroups

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Early_Islamic_Syria%2C_ca._640s.png/300px-Early_Islamic_Syria%2C_ca._640s.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Early_Islamic_Syria,_ca._640s.png)

The Yaman tribes, including the Banu Kalb, Ghassan, Judham and Tanukh, largely inhabited the districts of [Filastin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jund_Filastin "Jund Filastin"), [al-Urdunn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jund_al-Urdunn "Jund al-Urdunn") and [Hims](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jund_Hims "Jund Hims"), while the Qays inhabited [al-Jazirah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Upper_Mesopotamia "Upper Mesopotamia"), the [Byzantine frontier](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Awasim "Al-Awasim") and [Qinnasrin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jund_Qinnasrin "Jund Qinnasrin").

Arab tribes are prevalent in the Arabian Peninsula, Mesopotamia, Levant, Egypt, Maghreb, the Sudan region and Horn Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-284"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-284">[281]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Imagining_the_Arabs_:_Arab_identity_and_the_rise_of_Islam_282-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Imagining_the_Arabs_:_Arab_identity_and_the_rise_of_Islam-282">[279]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-285"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-285">[282]</a></sup>

The Arabs of the [Levant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Levant "Levant") are traditionally divided into [Qays and Yaman tribes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qays_and_Yaman_tribes "Qays and Yaman tribes"). The distinction between Qays and Yaman dates back to the pre-Islamic era and was based on tribal affiliations and geographic locations.; they include [Banu Kalb](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Banu_Kalb "Banu Kalb"), [Kinda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kinda_(tribe) "Kinda (tribe)"), [Ghassanids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghassanids "Ghassanids"), and [Lakhmids](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lakhmids "Lakhmids").<sup id="cite_ref-286"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-286">[283]</a></sup> The Qays were made up of tribes such as [Banu Kilab](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Banu_Kilab "Banu Kilab"), [Banu Tayy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tayy "Tayy"), [Banu Hanifa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Banu_Hanifa "Banu Hanifa"), and [Banu Tamim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Banu_Tamim "Banu Tamim"), among others. The Yaman, on the other hand, were composed of tribes such as [Banu Hashim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Banu_Hashim "Banu Hashim"), [Banu Makhzum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Banu_Makhzum "Banu Makhzum"), [Banu Umayya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umayyad_dynasty "Umayyad dynasty"), and [Banu Zuhra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Banu_Zuhrah "Banu Zuhrah"), among others.

There are also many Arab tribes indigenous to Mesopotamia (Iraq) and Iran, including from well before the [Arab conquest of Persia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_conquest_of_Persia "Arab conquest of Persia") in 633 CE.<sup id="cite_ref-IranicaDaniel2_287-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-IranicaDaniel2-287">[284]</a></sup> The largest group of [Iranian Arabs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iranian_Arabs "Iranian Arabs") are the [Ahwazi Arabs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahwazi_Arabs "Ahwazi Arabs"), including [Banu Ka'b](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Banu_Ka%27b "Banu Ka'b"), [Bani Turuf](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bani_Turuf "Bani Turuf") and the [Musha'sha'iyyah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Musha%27sha%27iyyah "Musha'sha'iyyah") sect. Smaller groups are the [Khamseh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Khamseh "Khamseh") nomads in [Fars Province](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fars_Province "Fars Province") and the [Arabs in Khorasan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs_in_Khorasan "Arabs in Khorasan"). As a result of the centuries-long [Arab migration to the Maghreb](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_migration_to_the_Maghreb "Arab migration to the Maghreb"), various Arab tribes (including [Banu Hilal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Banu_Hilal "Banu Hilal"), [Banu Sulaym](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Banu_Sulaym "Banu Sulaym") and [Maqil](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maqil "Maqil")) also settled in the Maghreb and formed the sub-tribes which exist to present-day. The [Banu Hilal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Banu_Hilal "Banu Hilal") spent almost a century in [Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egypt "Egypt") before moving to [Libya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Libya "Libya"), [Tunisia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tunisia "Tunisia") and [Algeria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algeria "Algeria"), and another century later moved to [Morocco](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morocco "Morocco").<sup id="cite_ref-288"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-288">[285]</a></sup>

According to Arab traditions, tribes are divided into different divisions called Arab skulls, which are described in the traditional custom of strength, abundance, victory, and honor. A number of them branched out, which later became independent tribes (sub-tribes). The majority of Arab tribes are descended from these major tribes.<sup id="cite_ref-289"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-289">[286]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-290"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-290">[287]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-المفصل_فى_تاريخ_العرب_قبل_الإسلام22_291-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-%D8%A7%D9%84%D9%85%D9%81%D8%B5%D9%84_%D9%81%D9%89_%D8%AA%D8%A7%D8%B1%D9%8A%D8%AE_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%B9%D8%B1%D8%A8_%D9%82%D8%A8%D9%84_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%A5%D8%B3%D9%84%D8%A7%D9%8522-291">[288]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-292"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-292">[289]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-293"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-293">[290]</a></sup>

They are:<sup id="cite_ref-المفصل_فى_تاريخ_العرب_قبل_الإسلام22_291-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-%D8%A7%D9%84%D9%85%D9%81%D8%B5%D9%84_%D9%81%D9%89_%D8%AA%D8%A7%D8%B1%D9%8A%D8%AE_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%B9%D8%B1%D8%A8_%D9%82%D8%A8%D9%84_%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%A5%D8%B3%D9%84%D8%A7%D9%8522-291">[288]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Banu_Adnan.png/300px-Banu_Adnan.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Banu_Adnan.png)

A family tree depicting the descendants of the Banu Adnan.

-   [Bakr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Banu_Bakr "Banu Bakr"), has descendants in Arabia and [Iraq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq "Iraq").<sup id="cite_ref-294"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-294">[291]</a></sup>
-   [Kinanah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kinana "Kinana"), has descendants in [Arabia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula "Arabian Peninsula"), [Iraq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq "Iraq"), [Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egypt "Egypt"), [Sudan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sudan "Sudan"), [Palestine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/State_of_Palestine "State of Palestine"), [Tunisia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tunisia "Tunisia"), [Morocco](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morocco "Morocco"), and [Syria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syria "Syria").<sup id="cite_ref-Brill2_295-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Brill2-295">[292]</a></sup>
-   [Hawazin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hawazin "Hawazin"), has descendants in [Arabia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula "Arabian Peninsula"), [Libya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Libya "Libya"), [Algeria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algeria "Algeria"), [Morocco](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morocco "Morocco"), [Sudan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sudan "Sudan"), and [Iraq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq "Iraq").<sup id="cite_ref-296"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-296">[293]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-297"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-297">[294]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-298"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-298">[295]</a></sup>
-   [Tamim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Banu_Tamim "Banu Tamim"), has descendants in [Arabia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula "Arabian Peninsula"), [Iraq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq "Iraq"), [Iran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iran "Iran"), [Palestine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Palestine_(region) "Palestine (region)"), [Algeria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algeria "Algeria"), and [Morocco](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morocco "Morocco")<sup id="cite_ref-299"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-299">[296]</a></sup>
-   [Azd](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Azd "Azd"), has descendants in [Arabia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula "Arabian Peninsula"), [Iraq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq "Iraq"), [Levant](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Levant "Levant"), and [North Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Africa "North Africa").<sup id="cite_ref-300"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-300">[297]</a></sup>
-   [Ghatafan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghatafan "Ghatafan"), has descendants in [Arabia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula "Arabian Peninsula") and the [Maghreb](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maghreb "Maghreb").<sup id="cite_ref-301"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-301">[298]</a></sup>
-   [Madhhij](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Madhhij "Madhhij"), has descendants in [Arabia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula "Arabian Peninsula") and [Iraq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq "Iraq").<sup id="cite_ref-302"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-302">[299]</a></sup>
-   [Abd al-Qays](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abd_al-Qays "Abd al-Qays"), has descendants in [Arabia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula "Arabian Peninsula").
-   [Al Qays](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Qays "Qays") (القيس), has descendants in [Arabia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula "Arabian Peninsula").
-   [Quda'a](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quda%27a "Quda'a"), has descendants in [Arabia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabian_Peninsula "Arabian Peninsula"), [Syria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Syria "Syria"), and [North Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Africa "North Africa").

## Geographic distribution

### Arab homeland

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Map_of_the_Arab_Diaspora_in_the_World.svg/386px-Map_of_the_Arab_Diaspora_in_the_World.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Map_of_the_Arab_Diaspora_in_the_World.svg)

Countries with significant Arab population and descendants.

  Arab world

  + 5,000,000

  + 1,000,000

  + 100,000

The total number of Arabs living in the [Arab nations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_League "Arab League") is estimated at 366 million by the [CIA Factbook](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CIA_Factbook "CIA Factbook") (as of 2014). The estimated number of Arabs in countries outside the Arab League is estimated at 17.5 million, yielding a total of close to 384 million. The Arab world stretches around 13,000,000 square kilometres (5,000,000 sq mi), from the [Atlantic Ocean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean "Atlantic Ocean") in the west to the [Arabian Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabian_Sea "Arabian Sea") in the east and from the [Mediterranean Sea](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea "Mediterranean Sea") in the north to the [Horn of Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Horn_of_Africa "Horn of Africa") and the [Indian Ocean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_Ocean "Indian Ocean") in the southeast.

### Arab diaspora

[Arab diaspora](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_diaspora "Arab diaspora") refers to descendants of the [Arab](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_people "Arab people") [immigrants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emigration "Emigration") who, voluntarily or as refugees, emigrated from their native lands in non-Arab countries, primarily in [East Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Africa "East Africa"), [South America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_America "South America"), [Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Europe "Europe"), [North America](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_America "North America"), [Australia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Australia "Australia") and parts of [South Asia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Asia "South Asia"), [Southeast Asia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southeast_Asia "Southeast Asia"), the [Caribbean](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Caribbean "Caribbean"), and [West Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Africa "West Africa"). According to the [International Organization for Migration](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_Organization_for_Migration "International Organization for Migration"), there are 13 million first-generation Arab migrants in the world, of which 5.8 million reside in Arab countries. Arab expatriates contribute to the circulation of financial and human capital in the region and thus significantly promote regional development. In 2009, Arab countries received a total of US$35.1 billion in [remittance](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Remittance "Remittance") in-flows and remittances sent to [Jordan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jordan "Jordan"), [Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egypt "Egypt") and [Lebanon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lebanon "Lebanon") from other Arab countries are 40 to 190 per cent higher than trade revenues between these and other Arab countries.<sup id="cite_ref-303"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-303">[300]</a></sup> The 250,000 strong Lebanese community in [West Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/West_Africa "West Africa") is the largest non-African group in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-304"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-304">[301]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-305"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-305">[302]</a></sup> Arab traders have long operated in [Southeast Asia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Southeast_Asia "Southeast Asia") and along the [East Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Africa "East Africa")'s [Swahili coast](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swahili_coast "Swahili coast"). [Zanzibar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zanzibar "Zanzibar") was once ruled by [Omani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Omanis "Omanis") Arabs.<sup id="cite_ref-306"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-306">[303]</a></sup> Most of the prominent [Indonesians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Indonesians "Arab Indonesians"), [Malaysians](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Malaysians "Arab Malaysians"), and [Singaporeans](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Singaporeans "Arab Singaporeans") of Arab descent are [Hadhrami people](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hadhrami_people "Hadhrami people") with origins in southern Arabia in the [Hadramawt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hadramawt "Hadramawt") coastal region.<sup id="cite_ref-307"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-307">[304]</a></sup>

#### Europe

Main articles: [Arabs in Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs_in_Europe "Arabs in Europe"), [Arabs in Austria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs_in_Austria "Arabs in Austria"), [Arabs in Bulgaria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs_in_Bulgaria "Arabs in Bulgaria"), [Arabs in Finland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs_in_Finland "Arabs in Finland"), [Arabs in France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs_in_France "Arabs in France"), [Arabs in Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs_in_Germany "Arabs in Germany"), [Arabs in Greece](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs_in_Greece "Arabs in Greece"), [Arabs in Italy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs_in_Italy "Arabs in Italy"), [Arabs in the Netherlands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs_in_the_Netherlands "Arabs in the Netherlands"), [Arabs in Romania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs_in_Romania "Arabs in Romania"), [Arabs in Serbia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs_in_Serbia "Arabs in Serbia"), [Arabs in Spain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs_in_Spain "Arabs in Spain"), [Arabs in Sweden](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs_in_Sweden "Arabs in Sweden"), [Arabs in Switzerland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs_in_Switzerland "Arabs in Switzerland"), [Arabs in Turkey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs_in_Turkey "Arabs in Turkey"), [British Arabs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Arabs "British Arabs"), [Arabs in Malta](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs_in_Malta "Arabs in Malta"), and [Arma people](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arma_people "Arma people")

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Dawn_Charles_V_Palace_Alhambra_Granada_Andalusia_Spain.jpg/200px-Dawn_Charles_V_Palace_Alhambra_Granada_Andalusia_Spain.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Dawn_Charles_V_Palace_Alhambra_Granada_Andalusia_Spain.jpg)

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/63/Institut_du_Monde_Arabe.jpg/200px-Institut_du_Monde_Arabe.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Institut_du_Monde_Arabe.jpg)

There are millions of [Arabs living in Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs_in_Europe "Arabs in Europe"), mostly concentrated in [France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/France "France") (about 6,000,000 in 2005<sup id="cite_ref-variety.com_308-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-variety.com-308">[305]</a></sup>). Most [Arabs in France](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs_in_France "Arabs in France") are from the [Maghreb](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maghreb "Maghreb") but some also come from the [Mashreq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mashreq "Mashreq") areas of the Arab world. Arabs in France form the second largest [ethnic group](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethnic_group "Ethnic group") after [French people](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_people "French people").<sup id="cite_ref-economist.com2_309-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-economist.com2-309">[306]</a></sup> In [Italy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Italy "Italy"), Arabs first arrived on the southern island of [Sicily](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sicily "Sicily") in the 9th century. The largest modern societies on the island from the Arab world are Tunisians and Moroccans, who make up 10.9% and 8% respectively of the foreign population of Sicily, which in itself constitutes 3.9% of the island's total population.<sup id="cite_ref-310"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-310">[307]</a></sup> The modern [Arab population of Spain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs_in_Spain "Arabs in Spain") numbers 1,800,000,<sup id="cite_ref-311"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-311">[308]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-312"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-312">[309]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-313"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-313">[310]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-314"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-314">[311]</a></sup> and there have been Arabs in [Spain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spain "Spain") since the early 8th century when the [Muslim conquest of Hispania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Umayyad_conquest_of_Hispania "Umayyad conquest of Hispania") created the state of Al-Andalus.<sup id="cite_ref-315"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-315">[312]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-316"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-316">[313]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-317"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-317">[314]</a></sup> [Arabs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs_in_Germany "Arabs in Germany") In [Germany](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Germany "Germany") the Arab population numbers over 1,401,950.<sup id="cite_ref-statista2_318-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-statista2-318">[315]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cz-herborn.de2_319-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-cz-herborn.de2-319">[316]</a></sup> in the [United Kingdom](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_Kingdom "United Kingdom") between 366,769<sup id="cite_ref-Naba11a2_320-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Naba11a2-320">[317]</a></sup> and 500,000,<sup id="cite_ref-321"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-321">[318]</a></sup> and in [Greece](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greece "Greece") between 250,000 and 750,000<sup id="cite_ref-Gre12_322-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Gre12-322">[319]</a></sup>). In addition, Greece is home to people from Arab countries who have the status of refugees (e.g. [refugees of the Syrian civil war](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Refugees_of_the_Syrian_civil_war "Refugees of the Syrian civil war")).<sup id="cite_ref-Kniffka19952_323-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Kniffka19952-323">[320]</a></sup> In the [Netherlands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Netherlands "Netherlands") 180,000,<sup id="cite_ref-auto2_40-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-auto2-40">[39]</a></sup> and in [Denmark](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denmark "Denmark") 121,000. Other countries are also home to Arab populations, including [Norway](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Norway "Norway"), [Austria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Austria "Austria"), [Bulgaria](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bulgaria "Bulgaria"), [Switzerland](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Switzerland "Switzerland"), [North Macedonia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Macedonia "North Macedonia"), [Romania](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Romania "Romania") and [Serbia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serbia "Serbia").<sup id="cite_ref-Arab_migration_facts_and_figures2_324-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Arab_migration_facts_and_figures2-324">[321]</a></sup> As of late 2015, [Turkey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkey "Turkey") had a total population of 78.7 million, with [Syrian refugees](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Refugees_of_the_Syrian_Civil_War "Refugees of the Syrian Civil War") accounting for 3.1% of that figure based on conservative estimates. Demographics indicated that the country previously had 1,500,000<sup id="cite_ref-ChapinMetz2_325-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-ChapinMetz2-325">[322]</a></sup> to 2,000,000 Arab residents,<sup id="cite_ref-www.aljazeera.com2_12-2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-www.aljazeera.com2-12">[12]</a></sup> [Turkey's Arab population](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs_in_Turkey "Arabs in Turkey") is now 4.5 to 5.1% of the total population, or approximately 4–5 million people.<sup id="cite_ref-www.aljazeera.com2_12-3"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-www.aljazeera.com2-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-www.washingtoninstitute.org2_326-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-www.washingtoninstitute.org2-326">[323]</a></sup>

#### Americas
