[Almaqah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Almaqah "Almaqah"), [Anbay](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Anbay "Anbay"), [ʿAṯtar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/%CA%BFA%E1%B9%AFtar "ʿAṯtar"), [Basamum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Basamum "Basamum"), [Dhu l-Khalasa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Demolition_of_Dhul_Khalasa "Demolition of Dhul Khalasa"), [Dushara](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dushara "Dushara"), [Haukim](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haukim "Haukim"), [Hubal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hubal "Hubal"), [Isāf and Nā'ila](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Is%C4%81f_and_N%C4%81%27ila "Isāf and Nā'ila"), [Manaf](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Manaf_(deity) "Manaf (deity)"), [Manāt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Man%C4%81t "Manāt"), [Nasr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nasr_(deity) "Nasr (deity)"), [Nuha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nuha_(deity) "Nuha (deity)"), [Quzah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quzah "Quzah"), [Ruda](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ruda_(deity) "Ruda (deity)"), [Sa'd](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sa%27d_(deity) "Sa'd (deity)"), [Shams, Samas](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shams_(goddess) "Shams (goddess)"), [Syn](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sin_(mythology) "Sin (mythology)"), [Suwa'](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Suwa%27 "Suwa'"), [Ta'lab](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ta%27lab "Ta'lab"), [Theandrios](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theandrios "Theandrios"), [al-‘Uzzá](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-%E2%80%98Uzz%C3%A1 "Al-‘Uzzá"), [Wadd](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wadd "Wadd"), [Ya'uq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ya%27uq "Ya'uq"), [Yaghūth](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yagh%C5%ABth "Yaghūth"), [Yatha](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yatha "Yatha"), [Aglibol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aglibol "Aglibol"), [Astarte](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Astarte "Astarte"), [Atargatis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atargatis "Atargatis"), [Baalshamin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baalshamin "Baalshamin"), [Bēl](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bel_(mythology) "Bel (mythology)"), [Bes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bes "Bes"), [Ēl, Ilāh](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/El_(deity) "El (deity)"), [Inanna/Ishtar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inanna "Inanna"), [Malakbel](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Malakbel "Malakbel"), [Nabū, Nebo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nabu "Nabu"), [Nergal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nergal "Nergal"), [Yarhibol](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yarhibol "Yarhibol").

### Philosophy

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Statue_of_Averroes_in_C%C3%B3rdoba%2C_Spain.jpg/150px-Statue_of_Averroes_in_C%C3%B3rdoba%2C_Spain.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Statue_of_Averroes_in_C%C3%B3rdoba,_Spain.jpg)

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/TCCKhaldun.jpg/134px-TCCKhaldun.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:TCCKhaldun.jpg)

Ibn Rushd (left), known in the west as [Averroes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Averroes "Averroes"), was a philosopher that influenced the rise of secular thought in Western Europe, while [Ibn Khaldun](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ibn_Khaldun "Ibn Khaldun") (right) was a sociologist, philosopher, and historian widely acknowledged to be one of the greatest social scientists of the Middle Ages.

The philosophical thought in the Arab world is heavily influenced by Arabic Philosophy. Schools of Arabic/Islamic thought include [Avicennism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avicennism "Avicennism") and [Averroism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Averroism "Averroism"). The first great Arab thinker in the Islamic tradition is widely regarded to be [al-Kindi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Kindi "Al-Kindi") (801–873 A.D.), a [Neo-Platonic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neo-Platonic "Neo-Platonic") philosopher, [mathematician](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematician "Mathematician") and [scientist](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scientist "Scientist") who lived in [Kufa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kufa "Kufa") and [Baghdad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baghdad "Baghdad") (modern day [Iraq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Iraq "Iraq")). After being appointed by the [Abbasid Caliphs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abbasid_Caliphs "Abbasid Caliphs") to translate [Greek](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greeks "Greeks") scientific and [philosophical](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philosophical "Philosophical") texts into [Arabic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabic "Arabic"), he wrote a number of original treatises of his own on a range of subjects, from [metaphysics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Metaphysics "Metaphysics") and [ethics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ethic "Ethic") to [mathematics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematic "Mathematic") and [pharmacology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pharmacology "Pharmacology").<sup id="cite_ref-498"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-498">[495]</a></sup>

Much of his [philosophical](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Philosophy "Philosophy") output focuses on [theological](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Theology "Theology") subjects such as the nature of [God](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/God "God"), the [soul](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soul "Soul") and [prophetic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prophecy "Prophecy") knowledge. Doctrines of the Arabic philosophers of the 9th–12th century who influenced medieval [Scholasticism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scholasticism "Scholasticism") in Europe. The Arabic tradition combines [Aristotelianism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aristotelianism "Aristotelianism") and [Neoplatonism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neoplatonism "Neoplatonism") with other ideas introduced through [Islam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam "Islam"). Influential thinkers include the non-Arabs [al-Farabi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Farabi "Al-Farabi") and [Avicenna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avicenna "Avicenna"). The Arabic philosophic literature was translated into [Hebrew](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hebrew_language "Hebrew language") and [Latin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Latin "Latin"), this contributed to the development of modern European philosophy. The Arabic tradition was developed by [Moses Maimonides](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Moses_Maimonides "Moses Maimonides") and [Ibn Khaldun](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ibn_Khaldun "Ibn Khaldun").<sup id="cite_ref-499"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-499">[496]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-500"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-500">[497]</a></sup>

### Science

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Houghton_Typ_620.47.452_-_Selenographia%2C_title.jpg/170px-Houghton_Typ_620.47.452_-_Selenographia%2C_title.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Houghton_Typ_620.47.452_-_Selenographia,_title.jpg)

[Hevelius](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hevelius "Hevelius")'s _[Selenographia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Selenographia "Selenographia")_, showing [Alhazen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alhazen "Alhazen") \[_[sic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sic "Sic")_\] representing reason, and [Galileo](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Galileo_Galilei "Galileo Galilei") representing the senses.

Arabic science underwent considerable development during the [Middle Ages](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Ages "Middle Ages") (8th to 13th centuries CE), a [source of knowledge that later spread throughout Medieval Europe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_world_contributions_to_Medieval_Europe "Islamic world contributions to Medieval Europe") and greatly influenced both medical practice and education. The language of recorded science was [Arabic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabic "Arabic"). Scientific treatises were composed by thinkers originating from across the [Muslim world](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim_world "Muslim world"). These accomplishments occurred after [Muhammad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad "Muhammad") united the Arab tribes and the spread of Islam beyond the Arabian peninsula.<sup id="cite_ref-501"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-501">[498]</a></sup>

Within a century after Muhammed's death (632 CE), an empire ruled by Arabs was established. It encompassed a large part of the planet, stretching from southern Europe to [North Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Africa "North Africa") to [Central Asia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Central_Asia "Central Asia") and on to [India](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India "India"). In 711 CE, Arab Muslims invaded southern Spain; [al-Andalus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Andalus "Al-Andalus") was a center of Arabic scientific accomplishment. Soon after, Sicily too joined the greater Islamic world. Another center emerged in [Baghdad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baghdad "Baghdad") from the Abbasids, who ruled part of the [Islamic world](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muslim_world "Muslim world") during a historic period later characterized as the "[Golden Age](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age "Islamic Golden Age")" (~750 to 1258 CE).<sup id="cite_ref-502"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-502">[499]</a></sup>

This era can be identified as the years between 692 and 945,<sup id="cite_ref-World_Civilization_Vol_1_1974,_pg._2342_503-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-World_Civilization_Vol_1_1974,_pg._2342-503">[500]</a></sup> and ended when the caliphate was marginalized by local Muslim rulers in Baghdad – its traditional seat of power. From 945 onward until the [sacking of Baghdad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sack_of_Baghdad "Sack of Baghdad") by the [Mongols](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mongol_invasions "Mongol invasions") in 1258, the Caliph continued on as a figurehead, with power devolving more to local subordinates.<sup id="cite_ref-World_Civilization_Vol_1_1974,_pg._2332_504-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-World_Civilization_Vol_1_1974,_pg._2332-504">[501]</a></sup> The pious scholars of Islam, men and women collectively known as the [ulama](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ulama "Ulama"), were the most influential element of society in the fields of [Sharia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sharia "Sharia") law, speculative thought and theology.<sup id="cite_ref-505"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-505">[502]</a></sup> Arabic scientific achievement is not as yet fully understood, but is very large.<sup id="cite_ref-RobinsonCambridge2_506-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-RobinsonCambridge2-506">[503]</a></sup> These achievements encompass a wide range of subject areas, especially [mathematics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics_in_medieval_Islam "Mathematics in medieval Islam"), [astronomy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Astronomy_in_medieval_Islam "Astronomy in medieval Islam"), and [medicine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medicine_in_medieval_Islam "Medicine in medieval Islam").<sup id="cite_ref-RobinsonCambridge2_506-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-RobinsonCambridge2-506">[503]</a></sup> Other subjects of scientific inquiry included [physics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Physics_in_medieval_Islam "Physics in medieval Islam"), [alchemy and chemistry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alchemy_and_chemistry_in_medieval_Islam "Alchemy and chemistry in medieval Islam"), [cosmology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cosmology_in_medieval_Islam "Cosmology in medieval Islam"), [ophthalmology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medieval_Islamic_ophthalmology "Medieval Islamic ophthalmology"), [geography and cartography](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geography_and_cartography_in_medieval_Islam "Geography and cartography in medieval Islam"), [sociology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sociology_in_medieval_Islam "Sociology in medieval Islam"), and [psychology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Psychology_in_medieval_Islam "Psychology in medieval Islam").<sup id="cite_ref-507"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-507">[504]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-508"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-508">[505]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Maqamat_hariri.jpg/220px-Maqamat_hariri.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Maqamat_hariri.jpg)

Illustration of scholars dating from the Abbasid period by [Yahya ibn Mahmud al-Wasiti](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yahya_ibn_Mahmud_al-Wasiti "Yahya ibn Mahmud al-Wasiti") from the _[Maqamat of Al-Hariri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maqamat_of_Al-Hariri_(manuscript) "Maqamat of Al-Hariri (manuscript)")_ manuscript.

[Al-Battani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Battani "Al-Battani") was an astronomer, astrologer and mathematician of the [Islamic Golden Age](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age "Islamic Golden Age"). His work is considered instrumental in the development of science and astronomy. One of Al-Battani's best-known achievements in astronomy was the determination of the solar year as being 365 days, 5 hours, 46 minutes and 24 seconds which is only 2 minutes and 22 seconds off.<sup id="cite_ref-MacTutor2_509-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-MacTutor2-509">[506]</a></sup> In [mathematics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_mathematics "Islamic mathematics"), al-Battānī produced a number of [trigonometrical](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Trigonometry "Trigonometry") relationships.<sup id="cite_ref-MacTutor2_509-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-MacTutor2-509">[506]</a></sup> [Al-Zahrawi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Zahrawi "Al-Zahrawi"), regarded by many as the greatest surgeon of the [Middle Ages](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_Ages "Middle Ages").<sup id="cite_ref-510"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-510">[507]</a></sup> His surgical treatise "[De chirurgia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Tasrif "Al-Tasrif")" is the first illustrated surgical guide ever written. It remained the primary source for surgical procedures and instruments in Europe for the next 500 years.<sup id="cite_ref-511"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-511">[508]</a></sup> The book helped lay the foundation to establish [surgery](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Surgery "Surgery") as a scientific discipline independent from [medicine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medicine "Medicine"), earning al-Zahrawi his name as one of the founders of this field.<sup id="cite_ref-512"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-512">[509]</a></sup>

Other notable Arabic contributions include among other things: the pioneering of [organic chemistry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Organic_chemistry "Organic chemistry") by [Jābir ibn Hayyān](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J%C4%81bir_ibn_Hayy%C4%81n "Jābir ibn Hayyān"),<sup id="cite_ref-513"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-513">[510]</a></sup> establishing the science of [cryptology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cryptology "Cryptology") and [cryptanalysis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cryptanalysis "Cryptanalysis") by [al-Kindi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Kindi "Al-Kindi"),<sup id="cite_ref-514"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-514">[511]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-515"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-515">[512]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-516"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-516">[513]</a></sup> the development of [analytic geometry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Analytic_geometry "Analytic geometry") by [Ibn al-Haytham](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ibn_al-Haytham "Ibn al-Haytham"),<sup id="cite_ref-517"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-517">[514]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-518"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-518">[515]</a></sup> who has been described as the "world's first true scientist",<sup id="cite_ref-519"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-519">[516]</a></sup> the discovery of the [pulmonary circulation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pulmonary_circulation "Pulmonary circulation") by [Ibn al-Nafis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ibn_al-Nafis "Ibn al-Nafis"),<sup id="cite_ref-520"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-520">[517]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-521"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-521">[518]</a></sup> the discovery of the [itch mite](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Itch_mite "Itch mite") parasite by [Ibn Zuhr](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ibn_Zuhr "Ibn Zuhr"),<sup id="cite_ref-522"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-522">[519]</a></sup> the first use of [irrational numbers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Irrational_numbers "Irrational numbers") as an algebraic objects by [Abū Kāmil](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ab%C5%AB_K%C4%81mil "Abū Kāmil"),<sup id="cite_ref-523"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-523">[520]</a></sup> the first use of the positional [decimal fractions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Decimal_fractions "Decimal fractions") by [al-Uqlidisi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abu%27l-Hasan_al-Uqlidisi "Abu'l-Hasan al-Uqlidisi"),<sup id="cite_ref-524"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-524">[521]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-525"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-525">[522]</a></sup> the development of the [Arabic numerals](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabic_numerals "Arabic numerals") and an early [algebraic symbolism](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_mathematical_notation "History of mathematical notation") in the [Maghreb](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maghreb "Maghreb"),<sup id="cite_ref-526"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-526">[523]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-527"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-527">[524]</a></sup> the [Thabit number](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thabit_number "Thabit number") and [Thābit theorem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amicable_numbers#Th%C4%81bit_ibn_Qurra_theorem "Amicable numbers") by [Thābit ibn Qurra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Th%C4%81bit_ibn_Qurra "Thābit ibn Qurra"),<sup id="cite_ref-Rashed2_528-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Rashed2-528">[525]</a></sup> the discovery of several new [trigonometric identities](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_trigonometric_identities "List of trigonometric identities") by [Ibn Yunus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ibn_Yunus "Ibn Yunus") and [al-Battani](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Battani "Al-Battani"),<sup id="cite_ref-529"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-529">[526]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-530"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-530">[527]</a></sup> the [mathematical proof](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_proof "Mathematical proof") for [Ceva's theorem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ceva%27s_theorem "Ceva's theorem") by [Ibn Hűd](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yusuf_al-Mu%27taman_ibn_Hud "Yusuf al-Mu'taman ibn Hud"),<sup id="cite_ref-531"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-531">[528]</a></sup> the first accurate [lunar model](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lunar_theory "Lunar theory") by [Ibn al-Shatir](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ibn_al-Shatir "Ibn al-Shatir"),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESaliba1994b233–234_&amp;_240_532-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-FOOTNOTESaliba1994b233%E2%80%93234_&amp;_240-532">[529]</a></sup> the invention of the [torquetum](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Torquetum "Torquetum") by [Jabir ibn Aflah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jabir_ibn_Aflah "Jabir ibn Aflah"),<sup id="cite_ref-533"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-533">[530]</a></sup> the invention of the universal [astrolabe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Astrolabe "Astrolabe") and the [equatorium](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Equatorium "Equatorium") by [al-Zarqali](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Zarqali "Al-Zarqali"),<sup id="cite_ref-534"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-534">[531]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-535"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-535">[532]</a></sup> the first description of the [crankshaft](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Crankshaft "Crankshaft") by [al-Jazari](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Jazari "Al-Jazari"),<sup id="cite_ref-536"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-536">[533]</a></sup> the anticipation of the [inertia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Inertia "Inertia") concept by [Averroes](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Averroes "Averroes"),<sup id="cite_ref-537"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-537">[534]</a></sup> the discovery of the [physical reaction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reaction_(physics) "Reaction (physics)") by [Avempace](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Avempace "Avempace"),<sup id="cite_ref-538"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-538">[535]</a></sup> the identification of more than 200 new [plants](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Plants "Plants") by [Ibn al-Baitar](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ibn_al-Baitar "Ibn al-Baitar")<sup id="cite_ref-539"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-539">[536]</a></sup> the [Arab Agricultural Revolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Agricultural_Revolution "Arab Agricultural Revolution"), and the [Tabula Rogeriana](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tabula_Rogeriana "Tabula Rogeriana"), which was the most accurate world map in pre-modern times by [al-Idrisi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al-Idrisi "Al-Idrisi").<sup id="cite_ref-bacharach2_540-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-bacharach2-540">[537]</a></sup>

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Al-jazari_water_device.jpg/170px-Al-jazari_water_device.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Al-jazari_water_device.jpg)

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Cheshm_manuscript.jpg/158px-Cheshm_manuscript.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Cheshm_manuscript.jpg)

Diagram of a hydro-powered perpetual flute from The Book of Knowledge of Ingenious Mechanical Devices by [Ismail al-Jazari](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ismail_al-Jazari "Ismail al-Jazari"), 1206. (left) The eye according to [Hunayn ibn Ishaq](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hunayn_ibn_Ishaq "Hunayn ibn Ishaq"), c.1200 (right)

The birth of the University institution can be traced to this development, as several universities and educational institutions of the Arab world such as the [University of Al Quaraouiyine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Al_Quaraouiyine "University of Al Quaraouiyine"), [Al Azhar University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Azhar_University "Al Azhar University"), and [Al Zaytuna University](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Ez-Zitouna "University of Ez-Zitouna") are considered to be the oldest in the world. Founded by [Fatima al Fihri](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fatima_al-Fihri "Fatima al-Fihri") in 859 as a mosque, the University of Al Quaraouiyine in [Fez](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fez,_Morocco "Fez, Morocco") is the oldest existing, continually operating and the first [degree](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Academic_degree "Academic degree") awarding educational institution in the world according to [UNESCO](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UNESCO "UNESCO") and [Guinness World Records](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Guinness_World_Records "Guinness World Records")<sup id="cite_ref-541"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-541">[538]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-542"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-542">[539]</a></sup> and is sometimes referred to as the oldest university.<sup id="cite_ref-543"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-543">[540]</a></sup>

There are many scientific [Arabic loanwords](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Influence_of_Arabic_on_other_languages "Influence of Arabic on other languages") in Western European languages, including [English](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Category:English_terms_derived_from_Arabic "wiktionary:Category:English terms derived from Arabic"), mostly via Old French.<sup id="cite_ref-544"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-544">[541]</a></sup> This includes [traditional star names](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Arabic_star_names "List of Arabic star names") such as [Aldebaran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aldebaran "Aldebaran"), scientific terms like _[alchemy](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/alchemy "wiktionary:alchemy")_ (whence also _[chemistry](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/chemistry "wiktionary:chemistry")_), _[algebra](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/algebra "wiktionary:algebra")_, _[algorithm](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/algorithm "wiktionary:algorithm")_, _[alcohol](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/alcohol "wiktionary:alcohol")_, _[alkali](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/alkali "wiktionary:alkali")_, _[cipher](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/cipher "wiktionary:cipher")_, _[zenith](https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/zenith "wiktionary:zenith")_, etc.

Under [Ottoman rule](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ottoman_rule "Ottoman rule"), cultural life and science in the Arab world declined. In the 20th and 21st centuries, Arabs who have won important science prizes include [Ahmed Zewail](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahmed_Zewail "Ahmed Zewail") and [Elias Corey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elias_Corey "Elias Corey") ([Nobel Prize](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nobel_Prize "Nobel Prize")), [Michael DeBakey](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_DeBakey "Michael DeBakey") and [Alim Benabid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alim_Louis_Benabid "Alim Louis Benabid") ([Lasker Award](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lasker_Award "Lasker Award")), [Omar M. Yaghi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Omar_M._Yaghi "Omar M. Yaghi") ([Wolf Prize](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wolf_Prize "Wolf Prize")), [Huda Zoghbi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Huda_Zoghbi "Huda Zoghbi") ([Shaw Prize](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shaw_Prize "Shaw Prize")), [Zaha Hadid](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zaha_Hadid "Zaha Hadid") ([Pritzker Prize](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pritzker_Prize "Pritzker Prize")), and [Michael Atiyah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Atiyah "Michael Atiyah") (both [Fields Medal](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fields_Medal "Fields Medal") and [Abel Prize](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abel_Prize "Abel Prize")). [Rachid Yazami](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rachid_Yazami "Rachid Yazami") was one of the co-inventors of the [lithium-ion battery](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lithium-ion_battery "Lithium-ion battery"),<sup id="cite_ref-545"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-545">[542]</a></sup> and [Tony Fadell](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tony_Fadell "Tony Fadell") was important in the development of the [iPod](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPod "IPod") and the [iPhone](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IPhone "IPhone").<sup id="cite_ref-546"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-546">[543]</a></sup>

### Theatre

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Yousef_wahby.jpg/170px-Yousef_wahby.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Yousef_wahby.jpg)

[Youssef Wahbi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Youssef_Wahbi "Youssef Wahbi"), (1898-1982) was a prominent Arab playwright, actor, and director who played a major role in shaping modern Arab theatre.

Arab theatre is a rich and diverse cultural form that encompasses a wide range of styles, genres, and historical influences. Its roots in the pre-Islamic era, when poetry, storytelling, and musical performances were the main forms of artistic expressionIt refers to theatrical performances that are created by Arab playwrights, actors, and directors. The roots of Arab theatre can be traced back to ancient [Arabic poetry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabic_poetry "Arabic poetry") and storytelling, which often incorporated music and dance. In the [early Arabic period](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Historiography_of_early_Islam "Historiography of early Islam"), storytelling evolved into a more formalized art form that was performed in public gatherings and festivals.<sup id="cite_ref-547"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-547">[544]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-548"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-548">[545]</a></sup>

During the [Islamic Golden Age](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age "Islamic Golden Age") in the 8th and 9th centuries, the city of [Baghdad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baghdad "Baghdad") emerged as a hub of intellectual and artistic activity, including theatre. The court of the Abbasid Caliphate was home to many influential playwrights and performers, who helped to develop and popularize theatre throughout the Islamic world. Arab theatre has a long tradition of incorporating comedy and satire into its performances, often using humor to address social and political issues.<sup id="cite_ref-549"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-549">[546]</a></sup>

Arab theatre encompasses a wide range of dramatic genres, including tragedy, melodrama, and historical plays. Many Arab playwrights have used drama to address contemporary issues, the role of [women in Arab society](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Women_in_the_Arab_world "Women in the Arab world"), and the challenges facing young people in the modern world. In recent decades, many Arab theatre artists have pushed the boundaries of the form, experimenting with new styles and techniques. This has led to the emergence of a vibrant contemporary theatre scene in many Arab countries, with innovative productions and performances that challenge traditional notions of Arab identity and culture.<sup id="cite_ref-550"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-550">[547]</a></sup>

### Fashion

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Six_cushions_from_Palestine.jpg/220px-Six_cushions_from_Palestine.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Six_cushions_from_Palestine.jpg)

Modern [cross-stitch](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cross-stitch "Cross-stitch") cushions. From top left, clockwise: [Gaza](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gaza_City "Gaza City"), [Ramallah](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ramallah "Ramallah"), Ramallah, [Nablus](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nablus "Nablus"), [Beit Jalla](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Beit_Jalla "Beit Jalla"), [Bethlehem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bethlehem "Bethlehem").

Arab fashion and design have a rich history and cultural significance that spans centuries, each with its unique fashion and design traditions. One of the most notable aspects of Arab fashion is the use of luxurious [fabrics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Textile "Textile") and intricate [embroidery](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Embroidery "Embroidery"). Traditional garments, such as the [Abaya](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abaya "Abaya") and [Thobe](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thawb "Thawb"), are often made from high-quality fabrics like [silk](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Silk "Silk"), [satin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Satin "Satin"), [brocade](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brocade "Brocade"), and are embellished with intricate embroidery and beading.<sup id="cite_ref-551"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-551">[548]</a></sup> In recent years, Arab fashion has gained global recognition, with designers like [Elie Saab](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elie_Saab "Elie Saab"), [Zuhair Murad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zuhair_Murad "Zuhair Murad"), and [Reem Acra](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reem_Acra "Reem Acra") showcasing their designs on international runways.<sup id="cite_ref-552"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-552">[549]</a></sup>

These designers incorporate traditional Arab design elements into their collections, such as ornate patterns, luxurious fabrics, and intricate embellishments. In addition to fashion, Arab design is also characterized by its intricate geometric [patterns](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pattern "Pattern"), [calligraphy](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_calligraphy "Arab calligraphy"), and use of vibrant colors. Arabic art and architecture, with their intricate geometric patterns and motifs, have influenced Arab design for centuries.<sup id="cite_ref-553"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-553">[550]</a></sup> Arab designers also incorporate traditional motifs, such as the paisley and the [arabesque](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabesque "Arabesque"), into their work. Overall, Arab fashion elements are rooted in the rich cultural heritage of the Arab world and continue to inspire designers today.<sup id="cite_ref-554"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-554">[551]</a></sup>

### Wedding and marriage

[![](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Tatouage_au_Henn%C3%A9%2C_Maroc.jpg/220px-Tatouage_au_Henn%C3%A9%2C_Maroc.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Tatouage_au_Henn%C3%A9,_Maroc.jpg)

[Henna](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Henna "Henna") tattoo in [Morocco](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Morocco "Morocco")

[Arabic weddings](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabic_wedding "Arabic wedding") have changed greatly in the past 100 years. Original traditional Arabic weddings are supposed to be very similar to modern-day [Bedouin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bedouin "Bedouin") weddings and rural weddings, and they are in some cases unique from one region to another, even within the same country. The practice of [marrying](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Marriage "Marriage") of relatives is a common feature of [Arab culture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_culture "Arab culture").<sup id="cite_ref-555"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-555">[552]</a></sup>

In the Arab world today between 40% and 50% of all marriages are [consanguineous](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consanguineous "Consanguineous") or between close family members, though these figures may vary among Arab nations.<sup id="cite_ref-556"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-556">[553]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-pmid242942992_557-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-pmid242942992-557">[554]</a></sup> In [Egypt](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Egypt "Egypt"), around 40% of the population [marry a cousin](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cousin_marriage "Cousin marriage"). A 1992 survey in [Jordan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jordan "Jordan") found that 32% were married to a first cousin; a further 17.3% were married to more distant relatives.<sup id="cite_ref-558"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-558">[555]</a></sup> 67% of marriages in [Saudi Arabia](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saudi_Arabia "Saudi Arabia") are between close relatives as are 54% of all marriages in [Kuwait](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kuwait "Kuwait"), whereas 18% of all [Lebanese](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lebanon "Lebanon") were between [blood relatives](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blood_relatives "Blood relatives").<sup id="cite_ref-Inbreeding2_559-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Inbreeding2-559">[556]</a></sup> Due to the actions of [Muhammad](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad "Muhammad") and the [Rightly Guided Caliphs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rightly_Guided_Caliphs "Rightly Guided Caliphs"), marriage between cousins is explicitly allowed in [Islam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Islam "Islam") and the [Quran](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quran "Quran") itself does not discourage or forbid the practice.<sup id="cite_ref-560"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-560">[557]</a></sup> Nevertheless, opinions vary on whether the [phenomenon](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Phenomenon "Phenomenon") should be seen as exclusively based on Islamic practices as a 1992 study among Arabs in Jordan did not show significant differences between [Christian Arabs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Christians "Arab Christians") or [Muslim Arabs](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_Muslims "Arab Muslims") when comparing the occurrence of [consanguinity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Consanguinity "Consanguinity").<sup id="cite_ref-Inbreeding2_559-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Inbreeding2-559">[556]</a></sup>

## Genetics

Arabs are diverse genetically as a result of their intermarriage and mixing with indigenous people of the pre-Islamic Middle East and North Africa following the Islamic expansion.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_561-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-:2-561">[558]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-562"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-562">[559]</a></sup> Genetic ancestry components related to the Arabian Peninsula display an increasing frequency pattern from west to east over North Africa. A similar frequency pattern exist across [northeastern Africa](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Northeast_Africa "Northeast Africa") with decreasing genetic affinities to groups of the Arabian Peninsula along the [Nile river valley](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nile "Nile") across [Sudan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sudan "Sudan") and [South Sudan](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/South_Sudan "South Sudan") the more they go south.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_563-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-:3-563">[560]</a></sup> This [genetic cline](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cline_(biology) "Cline (biology)") of admixture is dated to the time of [Arab expansion and immigration to the Maghreb](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_migrations_to_the_Maghreb "Arab migrations to the Maghreb") and northeast Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_563-1"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-:3-563">[560]</a></sup> Genetic research has indicated that Palestinian Arabs and [Jews](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jews "Jews") share common genetic ancestry and are closely related.<sup id="cite_ref-564"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-564">[561]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-565"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-565">[562]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Nebel2000_566-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Nebel2000-566">[563]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Behar2010_567-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Behar2010-567">[564]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-568"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-568">[565]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-569"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-569">[566]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-570"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-570">[567]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Nebel_2001_571-0"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-Nebel_2001-571">[568]</a></sup>

    -   Arabs share a strong bond through their ethnic, linguistic, and cultural heritage. This connection encompasses their history, nationalism, and geographic ties. Religion also influences it, contributing to its distinct customs, arts, cuisine, and societal identity.<sup id="cite_ref-75"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-75">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_note-76">[74]</a></sup>
    -   [Arab identity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arab_identity "Arab identity") concentrating on ethnic identity is another way of defining Arab identity, which can be subdivided into linguistic, cultural, social, historical, political, national, or genealogical terms.

116.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_ref-EoR-Ishmael_120-0 "Jump up")** Fredrick E. Greenspahn (2005). "Ishmael". In Lindsay Jones (ed.). [_Encyclopedia of Religion_](https://books.google.com/books?id=0jMOAQAAMAAJ&q=Ishmael). Vol. 7. Macmillan Reference USA. pp. 4551–4552. [ISBN](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISBN_(identifier) "ISBN (identifier)") [9780028657400](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780028657400 "Special:BookSources/9780028657400"). ISHMAEL, or, in Hebrew, Yishmaʿeʾl; eldest son of Abraham. Ishmael's mother was Agar, an Egyptian slave-girl whom Sarah had as her maid and eventually donated to Abraham because this royal couple were aged and childless but they were unaware then of God's plan and Israel; in accordance with Mesopotamian law, the offspring of such a union would be credited to Sarah (Gn. 16:2). The name Yishmaʿeʾl is known from various ancient Semitic cultures and means "God has hearkened," suggesting that a child so named was regarded as the answer to a request. Ishmael was circumcised at the age of thirteen by Abraham and expelled with his mother Agar at the instigation of Sarah, Abraham's wife, who wanted to ensure that Isaac would be Abraham's heir (Gn. 21). In the New Testament, Paul uses this incident to symbolize the relationship between Judaism and Christianity (Gal. 4:21–31). In the Genesis account, God blessed Ishmael, promising that he would be the founder of a great nation and a "wild ass of a man" always at odds with others (Gn. 16:12). So Abraham rose up in the morning, and taking bread and a bottle of water, put it upon her shoulder, and delivered the boy, and sent her away. And she departed, and wandered in the wilderness of Bersabee. \[15\] And when the water in the bottle was spent, she cast the boy under one of the trees that were there. Genesis chapter 21: \[16\] And she went her way, and sat over against him a great way off as far as a bow can carry, for she said: I will not see the boy die: and sitting over against, she lifted up her voice and wept. \[17\] And God heard the voice of the boy: and an angel of God called to Agar from heaven, saying: What art thou doing, Agar? fear not: for God hath heard the voice of the boy, from the place wherein he is. \[18\] Arise, take up the boy, and hold him by the hand: for I will make him a great nation. \[19\] And God opened her eyes: and she saw a well of water, and went and filled the bottle, and gave the boy to drink. \[20\] And God was with him: and he grew, and dwelt in the wilderness, and became a young man, an archer. \[21\] And he dwelt in the wilderness of Pharan, and his mother took a wife for him out of the land of Egypt. \[22\] At the same time Abimelech, and Phicol the general of his army said to Abraham: God is with thee in all that thou dost. \[23\] Swear therefore by God, that thou wilt not hurt me, nor my posterity, nor my stock: but according to the kindness that I have done to thee, thou shalt do to me, and to the land wherein thou hast lived a stranger. \[24\] And Abraham said: I will swear. \[25\] And he reproved Abimelech for a well of water, which his servants had taken away by force. \[26\] And Abimelech answered: I knew not who did this thing: and thou didst not tell me, and I heard not of it till today. \[27\] And Abraham took sheep and oxen and gave them to Abimelech: and both of them made a league. \[28\] And Abraham set apart seven ewe lambs of the flock. \[29\] And Abimelech said to him: What mean these seven ewe lambs which thou hast set apart? \[30\] But he said: Thou shalt take seven ewe lambs at my hand: that they may be a testimony for me, that I dug this well. \[31\] Therefore that place was called Bersabee: because there both of them did swear. \[32\] And they made a league for the well of oath. \[33\] And Abimelech, and Phicol the general of his army arose and returned to the land of the Palestines. But Abraham planted a grove in Bersabee, and there called upon the name of the Lord God eternal. \[34\] And he was a sojourner in the land of the Palestines many days. \[Genesis 21:1-34\]Douay Rheims Bible. He is credited with twelve sons, described as "princes according to their tribes" (Gn. 25:16), representing perhaps an ancient confederacy. The Ishmaelites, vagrant traders closely related to the Midianites, were apparently regarded as his descendants. The fact that Ishmael's wife and mother are both said to have been Egyptian suggests close ties between the Ishmaelites and Egypt. According to Genesis 25:17, Ishmael lived to the age of 137. Islamic tradition tends to ascribe a larger role to Ishmael than does the Bible. He is considered a prophet and, according to certain theologians, the offspring whom Abraham was commanded to sacrifice (although surah Judaism has generally regarded him as wicked, although repentance is also ascribed to him. According to some rabbinic traditions, his two wives were Aisha and Fatima, whose names are the same as those of Muhammad's wife and daughter Both Judaism and Islam see him as the ancestor of Arab peoples. Bibliography A survey of the Bible's patriarchal narratives can be found in Nahum M. Sarna's Understanding Genesis (New York, 1966). Postbiblical traditions, with reference to Christian and Islamic views, are collected in Louis Ginzberg's exhaustive Legends of the Jews, 2d ed., 2 vols., translated by Henrietta Szold and Paul Radin (Philadelphia, 2003). Frederick E. Greenspahn (1987 and 2005)

200.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_ref-:02_204-0 "Jump up")** \* [Herod](https://www.britannica.com/EBchecked/topic/263437/Herod) at _Encyclopædia Britannica_: "Herod was born in southern Palestine. His father, Antipater, was an Edomite (a Semitic people, identified by some scholars as Arab, who converted to Judaism in the 2nd century BCE). Antipater was a man of great influence and wealth who increased both by marrying the daughter of a noble from Petra (in southwestern Jordan), at that time the capital of the rising Arab Nabataean kingdom. Thus, Herod was of Arab origin, although he was a practicing Jew."
    
    -   Perowne, Stewart Henry (25 June 2015). ["Herod – king of Judaea"](https://web.archive.org/web/20150625081825/https://www.britannica.com/biography/Herod-king-of-Judaea). _Encyclopedia Britannica_. Archived from the original on 25 June 2015. Retrieved 22 November 2020.

214.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_ref-218 "Jump up")** ["Arabs"](http://www.iranicaonline.org/articles/abgar-dynasty-of-edessa-2nd-century-bc-to-3rd-century-ad) at _[Encyclopædia Iranica](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Encyclop%C3%A6dia_Iranica "Encyclopædia Iranica")_
    
    > The fame of Edessa in history rests, however, mainly on its claim to have been the first kingdom to adopt Christianity as its official religion. According to the legend current for centuries throughout the civilized world, Abgar Ukkama wrote to Jesus, inviting him to visit him at Edessa to heal him from sickness. In return he received the blessing of Jesus and subsequently was converted by the evangelist Addai. There is, however, no factual evidence for Christianity at Edessa before the reign of Abgar the Great, 150 years later. Scholars are generally agreed that the legend has confused the two Abgars. It cannot be proved that Abgar the Great adopted Christianity; but his friend Bardaiṣan was a heterodox Christian, and there was a church at Edessa in 201. It is testimony to the personality of Abgar the Great that he is credited by tradition with a leading role in the evangelization of Edessa.

These local inhabitants, in turn, were descendants of the core population that had lived in the area for several centuries, some even since prehistorical times (Gil 1992)... Thus, our findings are in good agreement with the historical record...

564.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_ref-568 "Jump up")** Atzmon, G; et al. (2010). ["Abraham's Children in the Genome Era: Major Jewish Diaspora Populations Comprise Distinct Genetic Clusters with Shared Middle Eastern Ancestry"](https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/pmc/articles/PMC3032072). _[American Journal of Human Genetics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Journal_of_Human_Genetics "American Journal of Human Genetics")_. **86** (6): 850–859. [doi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doi_(identifier) "Doi (identifier)"):[10.1016/j.ajhg.2010.04.015](https://doi.org/10.1016%2Fj.ajhg.2010.04.015). 565.  **[^](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabs#cite_ref-569 "Jump up")** Nebel (2000), quote: By the fifth century CE, the majority of non-Jews and Jews had become Christians by conversion ([Bachi](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roberto_Bachi "Roberto Bachi") 1974). The first millennium CE was marked by the immigration of Arab tribes, reaching its climax with the Moslem conquest from the Arabian Peninsula (633–640 CE). This was followed by a slow process of Islamization of the local population, both of Christians and Jews (Shaban 1971; Mc Graw Donner 1981). Additional minor demographic changes might have been caused by subsequent invasions of the Seljuks, Crusaders, Mongols, Mamelukes and Ottoman Turks. Recent gene-flow from various geographic origins is reflected, for example, in the heterogeneous spectrum of globin mutations among Israeli Arabs (Filon et al. 1994). Israeli and Palestinian Arabs share a similar linguistic and geographic background with Jews. (p.631) According to historical records part, or perhaps the majority, of the Moslem Arabs in this country descended from local inhabitants, mainly Christians and Jews, who had converted after the Islamic conquest in the seventh century CE (Shaban 1971; Mc Graw Donner 1981). These local inhabitants, in turn, were descendants of the core population that had lived in the area for several centuries, some even since prehistorical times (Gil 1992). On the other hand, the ancestors of the great majority of present-day Jews lived outside this region for almost two millennia. Thus, our findings are in good agreement with historical evidence and suggest genetic continuity in both populations despite their long separation and the wide geographic dispersal of Jews.(p.637)
